# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Consumer Fetch Request to Record Processing Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a Kafka consumer fetch request is built, sent, and processed back into ConsumerRecords in apache/kafka. Find Java source files implementing: the Fetcher request builder, the network poll, the fetch response parsing, and the ConsumerRecords population.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

55-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the Kafka consumer fetch request processing chain in the apache/kafka codebase. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components in the Fetch Chain

**Files involved:**
1. **Fetcher.java** - Consumer-specific fetcher that orchestrates the fetch process
2. **AbstractFetch.java** - Base fetch logic including request building and response handling
3. **FetchRequest.java** - Request builder for constructing fetch requests
4. **FetchResponse.java** - Response parsing from brokers
5. **FetchSessionHandler.java** - Manages incremental fetch sessions
6. **CompletedFetch.java** - Represents fetched partition data with record parsing
7. **FetchCollector.java** - Orchestrates conversion of CompletedFetch to ConsumerRecords
8. **ConsumerRecords.java** - Final consumer-facing records collection

## Processing Flow

1. **Request Building**: `Fetcher.sendFetches()` calls `AbstractFetch.prepareFetchRequests()` to determine which partitions need fetching
2. **Request Creation**: `AbstractFetch.createFetchRequest()` builds a `FetchRequest` using `FetchRequest.Builder.forConsumer()`
3. **Network Send**: Request is sent through ConsumerNetworkClient
4. **Response Handling**: `AbstractFetch.handleFetchSuccess()` receives the `FetchResponse` and creates `CompletedFetch` objects
5. **Buffering**: CompletedFetch objects are added to FetchBuffer
6. **Record Parsing**: `FetchCollector.collectFetch()` processes buffered fetches, calling `CompletedFetch.fetchRecords()`
7. **Deserialization**: Individual records are parsed by `CompletedFetch.parseRecord()`, which deserializes keys and values
8. **Final Collection**: Parsed `ConsumerRecord` objects are aggregated into `ConsumerRecords` and returned to the user
